And certain old people say that one should use a fire cautery resembling the razor, and heat it up and place it between the ribs, until it reaches that abscess; and fever leaves pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse according to what we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not benefit, then I add three methods of cauterization that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Here is the translation:
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After placing the two inflamed nerves so that the keys are perceived from the other side, and then treat the fire cauterization, and thus there will be four; if you see, so cauterize all the cauterization to three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has taken place over long time, and this is true for the other cures previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cauterization does not benefit the dropsical, except by the method which is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure it according to the methods that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations around the mouth, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the kidneys, and two behind the back on the spine, and one near the breastbone; and let the cauterizations be well close to the space of the key.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After that, let the cautery remain open to generate healing for a long time, and do not cease the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing would hasten, and both intentions would be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the one that we have shown before as a clavicle; and the one for the back is olive-shaped, according to what has been placed here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsical, and are full of yellowish dew, it is necessary that you apply a cauter to the back of the foot between the thumb and index finger; and lift your hand with the cauter so as not to turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too far in, lest the yellowish dew bursts forth, and shape the cauter according to this form.
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make two cauteries on each leg at the tip of the little finger; and let the cauteries be long, one below the kneecap in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without curing, until the yellowish water is released; after that, cure with the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the uterine solution comes from coldness and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are relaxed, and cannot be cured by methods of cures; and you see the patient suffering strongly and having great virtue, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said here before or the stomach cautery, at the circulatory cautery; and three subtlety cauteries around the belly, each as fine as a clavicle, and two cauteres on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the thumb, and one cautery on each kneecap, and two small cauteres on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemroids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and consist of large, cold, moist, corrupt humors, and they are treated as we have said in divisions, but it does not help, then apply cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that part which is entirely beneath the almace date and little by little triangle-shaped, and one under the jaw, two fingers' breadth; and if you think his stomach is chilled, and the food is not cooked, and his face swells, then on his face apply a great cauterization on the stomach, as said before, and another on the liver, and another on the navel to all the cauterization of nail length; and let the cauter stay long.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure let the limb be so long as it is sound.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fatness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut to the fatness which is called "thelul", if you scrape off the cautery that appears as a razor, and then put it all ablaze on that fatness being cut; and leave your hand so long until the cauterizers come out at the birth of the vein, from which blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much fatness, then cauterize each one just as we have said; after curing with ointments for as long as they are healed; and if you cauterize a great cautery on the navel, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an uncured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes a disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes to anyone, and it is inflamed and discharges putrid matter and corrupted moisture, then you must test all the tent's subtlety, and know how deep it goes in the tent.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After apply the cautery which seems to be rough, and plug it into the fistula according to the amount that the tent has entered, and repeat the cautery until the putrid and corrupted flesh is burned away, once or twice or three times, depending on the quantity of what is needed; and beware of burning the nerve that are nearby, and great veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the bladder and into the intestine, then beware of those places, and do not make fires except in a charred place, and think it is not perilous; after cure let the limb be so long as it is sound, and if the flesh is seared, and the matters are removed for a long time, then know that the flesh is healed entirely; and if the matters are not removed, know that the flesh is torn, and corrupted bone at its root; and thus as one of those things which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of cold comes to the kidneys, and from excessive moisture, and does not take shape like a woman's, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the kidneys from one side and the other at the cautery clavicle which we have said before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizers in a line, and they will cause greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the part behind the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic hair begin, and one to the right and one to the left, and each cautery be as long as a thumb's breadth; and make one cautery behind the back, or two if you need them; and the cauterizers be clavicle-shaped according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the uterus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not leave a means for conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are delayed; and when they come, one feels great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauterizers around the mouth, as we said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizers behind the back; and be the cauterizers clavicle-shaped, as we said.
de la hainche	of the groin
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends to the groin of the haunch, and because of this, it moves from its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the wound of departure is found, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the groin of the haunch with one cautery resembling a circle, and sign in front of the wound around the groin as it turns, so that the groin is inside the circle; and let the cauterizers be such as those which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizers are not present, make three large cauterizers of the olivaire, and let them be as deep as all the colors; and cure until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin of the haunch, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the patient is cured with what we have said in the division and the cure does not hold, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors by fetid pills or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many manners, of which one is such: that you cauterize on the boil of the groin three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make good profundity and greatness, and have between each cautery the breadth of a thumb, and be the cauteries olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle above the head of the groin, for which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that it should be cauterized at the cautery of the circle which we said before in the dislocation of the haunch; but make it in this manner so that the circle contains all the haunch and all the spaces of the color are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that is the manner in which one does it in sciatica, when the pain holds in the groin and does not reach as far as the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, make two cauteries on each side where the patient says the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle four thumbs apart, slightly to the left; and be the cauteries knife-shaped, and let the depth of the burn be that of a key; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as the toes or almost there, make three or four cauteries at the point where they feel the pain, which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, make more; and if it seems that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then make a cautery at the cutellaire or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauterizers that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause more great nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have had a fire treatment on the ankle of the foot, and let it be until the leg was entirely swollen, and the feet as well, and were pierced and corrupted all the feet.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purging of the belly which caused his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, do a fire treatment on one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men say in the cauterization of the groin, why is it like this, make such an iron and let it be as big as a walnut of dactyl, or about one less, and be between the interstices and be from one interstice to another the length of a pod of peas; and the interstices are divided into two parts, and they are also like hazelnuts, and there is a good iron made; and that is the form.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be scalded until it is entirely red and gives off sweet smells, and then put on the boil of the sick person's backside, and be turned over on the healthy side; and have one fire cauterization repeated and leave it three days; and then make a poultice with butter, and let the wound remain open for a long time; after the cure by anointing until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use a little of this cauterization due to the fear of its gaze, and if we see none who use it; and yet these are good cauterizations, which can be borne by those where it is applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burning is such that you make an instrument with interlocking parts where the edges of the door descend, and it be made of earth or iron to a length of one pace, and in the upper part have two nozzles, and between each one have the quantity of the thickness of a dove; and they be over and under, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Then place the bed of hay under the patient lying on their chest, and after that lift your hand above the bed of hay; then pour between the two circles of hot water that has been heated over a fire one pot, and let it leave for an hour or a tenth, and allow the patient to feel the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds a burning or biting sensation like fire; and when the biting is past, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the warm hay bed, and let it be thus for three days, and put on butter until that which is black from scarring is removed; and let it rest for three days before applying ointment again as long as they are healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the hip or leg, make the instrument that holds it according to what you have done in the groin similarly; and this is the manner of warm poultice, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline and hot sulfur, equal amounts of each, and grind them together, and put them in a new vessel.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small opening for it to drain so that the point of a razor can go in; and put this pot into another well-filled one, and place sweet dew on top of the alkaline and sulfur, until you have two layers of powder above what you will take with your hand; and leave it thus until the aqueous humor and bile descend into the lower pot, then take all that awe and pour it onto sulfur and alkaline just as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very painful and administered in the movements of medical work and other cauterizations of limbs. For it does a good deed like fire, and if to other medicines that one cauterizes well the skin so as to use them thus, with honey, anacardium, and chalces with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us about a cure of which one man was cured of the pain in his skin and sciatic vein, and greatly praised it, saying that no other cure was done, and he became healthy at one time when this cure was made, and he bathed himself as it teaches hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in the same manner that you take green and dry lapis lazuli, and grind it much with a little bit of grease, and put it on the skin, and on the thigh, and on the leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it for three hours or until the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter the bath until his body is somewhat warm, and make him enter the bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a fire cautery of such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's hair fire, it helps a lot; and one must make the cauteries in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and put it on the hollow that is between the thumb of the foot and the other one which is called foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards take goat's hair which is dry, and put it on the fire until it is charred, and place it on the linen, and let it stay until it cools; and do this again, and do not stop doing so until you think by reason that it will reach as far as the hankle, and that the pain will cease; and this manner of cautery is called "goat's hair fire".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or percussion or from excessive evacuation or from similar cold matter spread out, none of these likenesses is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary afterwards that the patient be freed from fetid pills or similar things, and one makes signs on the back where the pain stays, three lines marked with an "enche", and in each line five or more cauterizations depending on the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and make the cauterization according to the cauterization called "poins"; and if you see, do three or four cauterizations at the cauterizing point middle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight, thin skin when they rise, and fear; and you will find in the last vertebra of the back and on our appearance which appears above other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you know how to cure it, then cauterize at the cauterizing point of that according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery penetrates each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine at the fire that pricks 2 lines or 3, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the wound is healed as we have said, and be careful that you do not administer a cautery in a swollen place which is near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is due to moistors that are spread out in each member of the body, and when pain comes into feet, which physicians properly call "podagre", and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterizations in this manner: make many cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then make the cautery all around as one says "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knees and at other joints, and this often happens, then make a cautery on each knee 3 or 4 times for each part, all around the olive-shaped area; and if you need more, do more, but don't hold your hand back longer than until the flesh of the key is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist II lines; and if there remains no pain at all, make incisions above each joint and above the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the shoulders or the armpits, cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you take good care of him and purge phlegm, he will be healed by the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the corruption of the scab
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When itch comes to pustules, and the boils descend to the groin and it is new, then it is necessary that when you see it cured, he does not annoy me that day; and that he uses things which loosen his bowels, so that the evil descends from his belly; after make him sit on his back between my hands, and command him to hold his breath until the boils are healed, and then cauterize below the itch on the bone of the elbow, and mark a sign like a half-circle above the body; then scald the cauterization in this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until he is pale and ejects stool.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then straighten the bowels to their place; and hold his hand above so that they do not return; and work well on the patient's hips, and put one cushion and one servant under him, and another under the breast which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign of the whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it at the first time, start again as many times as needed to reach the bone; and be careful subtly that the bowels do not burst when you make the cautery; so that you do not burn him; and so that through this the patient does not die, or suffer some other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come just to the bone with the fire cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children are subtle according to their measure, and those of great people also great according to their measure; after three days, care for the bone at the site of the cautery so that the scabbing is removed; afterwards, care for other ointments until they are healed, and have the patient lie on their back for 40 days until the wound is well sewn; and it is necessary that his stitches be loosened long enough, so that the bowels do not protrude when he will wish to go to chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wishes to rise up, have a well-made bandage applied to him, and keep it on for another 40 days; and let him have good rest, lest he trouble himself too much and take care not to drink or eat too much and not to cough loudly; and when he has followed this instruction, then is he entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter the surgery of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the itch of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come to other wounds and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then do the fire cautery on the fire as needed according to its quantity, and let it burn the third part of the key; after the cure according to what we have said; and some of the old ones have said that one should cauterize at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but mark the first point at the beginning and draw a line across the ulcer's width above it, and another below it, and then insert your hand into the entire cautery carefully.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are more gentle and subtle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, whether from falling or striking, and this pain persists for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not effective, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "points", and the cauterization should be according to the length of the member, its thinness, weakness, and virtue, and its location in terms of torments and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cauterization, that's well; if not, start another cauterization on it, for such a case is that he should be changed to the member that is closest to him, so you must make the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of sickness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The members are helped sometimes by cauterization with great help, and likewise the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can't you see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it's cured according to what we said in the division, and doesn't descend or remain, and you doubt that the corruption won't spread throughout the patient, then make V cauterizations on the head: I in the middle of the head up to nine, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and II on both horns, and I behind on the back; and leave your hand so that the cauterization comes as far as the bone, and so that the scales come out if the vapors of gross humors can issue forth; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is beforehand.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is spread everywhere; and it is manifestly failing, then it is necessary that you cauterize with those cauteries we have said on the head, and 1 cauterization behind the nape of the neck, and 2 cauteries on the spine of the neck, and 6 cauteries on the spine of the back, and 1 great one on the hump and another below, and 2 on each shoulder; and 2 on the sides, and 2 on the tendons of the breast, and 1 on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and take heed of the nerves that are behind the calcant, lest you burn them; and sometimes make a cauterization on the bone of the shoulder-blade, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more I do with a cautery, the more it helps him, and shows its benefit; and know that the patient does not feel any pain from the cautery just as the healthy person feels, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that the cautery be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the manner of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterwards, wash it with flour mixed with honey and other remedies until he is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, and he is not yet healed, then make a cautery on the member according to its greatness or smallness; and let the cautery be just a little bit into the flesh of the member; then treat it with ointments until he is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes one makes a cautery at the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is taken out the swelling; and yet no one intervenes unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the issues of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "ulcers" is inflamed, and the art of medicine is worth nothing, then one cauterizes with a cauterization a little deep, according to the quantity of the flesh of the vein, until the blenchour is removed, and its color changes; then apply a poultice made with flour of vetches and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of colander and almond, each one in equal parts; and mix everything together, and tie it up with a cloth, and air it at the bedside until he is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for syphilis by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre comes at the beginning, and you want to stop it, then cauterize around the channel with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the perimeter of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise men say that one should also make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; and yet it does not seem to me good, because I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already experienced this once; and more rightly is it that it should be cauterized around, with a cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be killed
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», and elle tarde de meurer or por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait or por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est à dire trop vieux) and il a peu de sang, ou por le temps; and tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize around of many small cauterizations in piercing; after that, he leaves it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it hastens to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the entire cauterization, then heat the cauterization so that its form is:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the midst of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauterizations have pierced through the skin, and be such cauterizations that the patient feels them externally in such a way that the course of the pus is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterward, care for him until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of sickness is called "corrodens", and it's nothing else than a consumption of member, for it consumes members just like fire consumes dry threads.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this sickness in a place that can suffer fire and cautery together, then use small and great clavicles of cauterization according to the place where the disease is; after cauterizing all parts until you have removed all corruption, and none remains, except what is consumed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put oil on the cauterized areas to soothe them, until all the burn blisters caused by fire are removed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of ointments generates flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it's good; and if not, then reapply the cautery to what remains of the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy is sometimes cured by medical treatment in place of fire cautery; but all the same, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of the medical treatment in its division: take what you need when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of pins which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often happens that at the end of the foot a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large defect that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization for this disease is done in two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to know fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat the cautery iron as hot as a tile oven, and it should be made of good iron to its measure so that it can pierce the nail from all sides, and there are fine edges; afterwards put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand completely around the nail until it comes to the end of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to rot; then apply a poultice of wild marjoram crushed with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall off and be detached from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat the joint with ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by external wounds to the body, and many times happen in hands and feet, it is necessary that you bring a water cauterization; and do thus: take a bronze or iron tube, or a vulture's feather, and put it on the wart and all its warts; and place the tube so that it surrounds everything, then put a little hot water in it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand as you turn, so that the edge of the tube reaches the root of the wart, and can find the hot water's way to the root; and let the patient suffer a little the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will uproot itself entirely with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So do one after another, until you have reached all those who are inside the body, then cure the swellings that bring forth flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cures of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people shiver from cold or heat, or quartan fever, or another, then you must make four cauterizations on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the belly, and one above the stomach at the olive-shaped cauterization; if the patient shivers, and the healthiness of the cold disease will hasten.
des pustules puans	the stinking pimples
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	At times, appearances become apparent on the outside of the body, or pustules that stink, which come from great corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is necessary at first when they appear that one makes a fire cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made from mulberry wood, by which the point is seized by the fire, or a long root of aristologe, or a lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at times when the cauterized ones are treated from the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further forward, but the superfluous parts that come from them are broken off and healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times it happens that great flows of blood come from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to someone, if you hasten to put your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and hold them tight until the blood is appeased beneath your fingers, and no more drips; then take a few small and large cauterizations, all red from fire, and take one, either great or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and put it on that vein which you are holding with your two fingers, and hold the cautery thus until the blood is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spouts forth when you lift your fingers from the vein, and the cauterization is extinguished, then take quickly another one of the cauterizations that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after another until the blood is staunched; and take care that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well staunched without one of the three ways we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong bandaging with thread, or by medicines placed on which have the power to stop blood; and let it be tied and strained in a suitable manner.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about the stanching by binding tightly with cloths or by placing hot things on it, or other similar things, if there is no benefit whatsoever.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he has no mirror or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein just as we have said, and stretch them well until it is staunched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move his hand, but moisten with cold water often enough so that the blood is congealed, thickened, and staunched; and make inquiries ahead about what he needs in terms of cauterizations and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in our first chapter all the diseases in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicine, and the remedies and causes and instruments and forms of cauterizations; and I have placed that chapter from head to feet, and I will go on in this chapter by the same way for those who want to find things more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, dear friend, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and therefore it is necessary to exercise greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to attempt foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come to cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who suffer so much with their illness that they will die quickly due to the distress they find in their disease, and the greatness of their malice; and one should have fear of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are some among these who give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your covetise, and do not rashly but wisely of what you are certain and can take hold of, and use prophesy and indication in the cures of your patients for whose salvation may be converted; and thus it will help you to achieve good renown, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Here is the translation:
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter in describing chapter by chapter, according to what is before the chapter of cauteries, which I have described from the beginning to the end, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Two full heads of water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often afflicts children at childbirth, and when the midwife constrains too tightly the head of the child; and sometimes it comes from a reason unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur except in children, and all those that I have seen died quickly; and therefore it seems to me that it is best to hasten the work in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head grew bigger each day until it could no longer be sustained; and believed so much moisture that he would die, and this moisture is assembled below the bone above the forehead, between the skull and the bone; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you cut a wide incision in the head's midst; and let it be as long as two inches, until the moisture runs out; and look at the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are the commissures of the head opening on each side, and the water jumps forth when you press it with your hand from inside, and it does not respond to you: then it is necessary that you make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After binding the wounds with cloth and powders, and putting vinegar and oil in, and leaving it thus until the fifth day; then loosen it, and treat the wound by tents and ointments, and let the head become dry, and only give food to the patient to eat dry meat with as little moisture as possible until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look where the great opening of the abscess appears, and the assembly of water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes to the right; and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then at the place where the abscess opens, and the filling of water, and make the incision according to what you are able; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and if there comes a flow of blood, so that the patient may die from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease which is called "catarre" in the eyes or at the breast, and the disease is old, and the treatment of medicine does not help at all, then the final cure is the cautery with what one will cut off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, then, when you see the wounds covered, that the patient makes his head go back; after which he should rub the place with a rough cloth so much that the arteries appear, then have the patient remove his neck from the entire cloth; then look and see if the vein bleeds, and the pulses of one and the other are afterwards above the ears, and they should be responded; then mark the pulses by pointing, then cut both with an acicular spatula to two parts, so much that the edge of the scalp comes to the bone, and it is done in a wide area.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the spatula below the artery and cut above it, cutting just as two would crosswise.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will jump out continuously outside.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to sensation, so it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then sign and stop at the bone; and what is needed for blood to be put outside is six times, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point of the sphac, so cut off that apostemes do not come there, then stop the wound and bind, and the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes, and sharp catarrh, because of the moisture of tears and heats in the temples and old forgotten and similar things, and it is treated by ways of medical cures and all that does not help at all, then we cut off the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient bends back his temples' hairs, and listens to the artery which appears in the temple, for it opens well with its beating, and is not responsive except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responsive, then extract the patient's neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and rise the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which there is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the leather lightly until you come to the artery, then train it upwards with tweezers, and depart well from each layer that is below each part; and if the artery is fine, so turn it to the point of the needle, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Because if it's not cut, then blood does not flow fully at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the blood of .vi. c., up to .iii.; and if the artery is large, then it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk, so that no purulence may come before the healing of the wound, and there be decorremens of blood; then cut off the superfluity which is between the two ties at that very hour, and then, if you see, cauterize the remaining part with the cautery knife up to the bone until the arteries are cut off; and this is the main work, if the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is help to finish the moistures: therefore it is of greater aid to the moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and puts a well-made tent on top; and when one removes them, be careful with dry medicines that bring forth flesh and tents until they are healed; and if there is no cort of the artery as long as you work, then hasten to cauterize by cautery, or take vitriol and strain it in your hand so that the blood is staunched; and if you do not have this present, put your finger on top of the place until the blood congeals, and rise the place with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be strained as necessary; and what is most important and lighter in the extraction of arteries is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting into two parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to keep their heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too thick, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two cutlery pieces a space of a good thumb's length, and then when you have signed to join the two parts, and you must put the hot iron on so that it reaches just to the bone, and make the incision in two places; and be distant between the two joints because this cautery is not done from top to bottom; and this is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are flowing down from the veins that are above the forehead of the head, and it does not benefit at all from the medicine that is done there, and you see the face of the patient growing red, and feeling the forehead to be agitated as if with fear; and the skin is tender and moist so that the hairs of the paper are fallen, and the papers are scorched by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary for this cure.
