Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the head of the nose, and grows and becomes great in time, until it is visible to look at; and therefore you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all impurities, then put the cautery or burning medicine on top; and if one delays cutting it as long as it is great, be wary if it is hard, of foul color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touchment, not of foul color, and you see that you can remove all of it, empty the patient's head and cut without fear, and cure the head with things restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Knows that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these joint works, it profits little, more so than in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore that you do as follows with each one, if you examine whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together to a seam, then care for it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, it is necessary that you scrape away all the parts of their crust until they heal, then bring the two lips together to a seam, and bind it, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and incense upon it; and place a piece of strong or another kind of plaster on top, and let it be for as long as it cures by itself, then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the seam is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the seam of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known.
des apostemes des levres	of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have within their lips abscesses hard, resembling grains of millet, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut on each notch, and take as pincers and cut in each part; then apply a poultice to the lip after the incision of vitriol, until the blood is staunched; and then anoint with oil, and cure the lip with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a wart grows on the gums that the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you support it with tweezers, and cut at its root, and let the blood or pus flow; then put on top of the wound vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders; and if that wart returns after the incision, and many times happens, then cut it again, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the sorors (sorores)
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are assembled in the chief of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, as corruption comes to the gum, and they are the teeth that stink; therefore it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his teeth be in thy sight, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, until there remains nothing; and thus do with the blackness and yellowness, and jaundice and other blemishes, until they are cleaned away; and if one removes what is at the first stage, it is good; but if not, then one renews the second day and the third, until you have removed all; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because those who pluck out the teeth to remove decayed teeth have different forms than those who remove between the teeth; and these forms and others be prepared with thee.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth's pain that you wait to draw it out as long as you can, for this should not be done quickly; for it is a very high substance so that there is no excuse for drawing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is forced to pull out, you must be certain about the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	The patient's pain continues many times, and he thinks it is from the tooth of Saint Denis, and makes a good attempt to pull out the tooth; but in any case, the pain does not depart on this account until the evil thing has come out, for we have already learned to do so with these saints; and when you are well certain about the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with a spatula as hard as possible to protect the gum from all sides; then move it to your two or tenaciously fine pincers at the first pace and pace, until it is well extracted; then secure the pincers well; and the patient's jaw should be in your holy place between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump out, then take one of these instruments and push it inside from each side lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and wounded, it is necessary that you fill it with cloths, where the perforation is; and if it is strained subtly with pincers, that it does not break while being strained; and it is necessary to work very carefully around the gum for dislodging the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And make sure that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and the tooth will come back to the patient through the evil of the root, causing greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act like ignorant surgeons, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the jaw, and do not bring back what we have told; but often bring great harm through the roots that remain, or through the jaw they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is torn out, wash the place with wine, vinegar, and gall; and if blood comes forth, which often happens, fill the place with powdered vitriol; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one should extract teeth first, are to be long-pointed and thick-handled, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be made of thick handles so that they do not bend when pulling out, and be made of well-forged iron, and have teeth to hold firmly in place.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains at the shoulder, it is necessary that you place a moistened cotton cloth on the spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the skin is softened, then put in forceps called "algefri", so that the head seems to be well-groomed; and let them be made inside just like a file, and that's their form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with all these pincers, it is necessary that you uncover the cart entirely around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is to know palying, of which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with these things, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the shapes come after this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you aid with this instrument that has two springs, of which this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like great pincers, whose shape is this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument should be made so that it cannot break; and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and wise and subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their works and the disease demonstrate, for there are such diseases where the ancient ones did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of cases, and if one breaks the cartilage or the other bones, or it can, then seek out the instruments that you need, which I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, whose shape is this:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be big and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore the area with medicines suitable for this, and if there is putridity in the bone, and it is small, then reduce it with all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form and the shape is ugly, especially in young girls, it is necessary that you know whether the tooth is born after the tooth and is not in its proper place, and cannot be shaved or filed: then extract it; and if it is attached to the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is this, and which resembles a small beak, and be made of well-forged iron with a point:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping goes slowly and slowly in hands of days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others; and if it appears to be able to be filed, then file it with a similar file whose shape is this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth slowly and slowly in hands of days lightly, so that it does not move until it is trimmed; then make it even at the end with any scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, then file away the roughness as long as it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is loose, either by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press down on what they are eating without it falling out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines and that doesn't work; so they must be restrained with a gold thread, because silver sons become green and perish, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see aligning the teeth, then take the thread and put it double between two healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth between my teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume the covering up to the part where you started, and strain your hand subtly and carefully, until it does not move anymore; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the end of the thread to a pair of forceps, and assemble it, and reattach it between two healthy teeth, so that it does not injure the tongue; then leave it thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the threads break, then bind it with another thread; it will thus remain and serve for a whole time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the alignment of two healthy teeth and two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Et when the tooth falls out, if one puts it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and does not intervene except by someone who is wise and patient, and sometimes makes the shape of a whalebone tooth, and puts it where the defect is, and holds it tight like we have said, and remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to bind the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is no instance where this thread comes from under the tongue or by nature; it arises either when someone is born that way or by accident of a wound being sutured; and the work is such that you work on the mouth of the patient, with their head in your healthy one, and lift up the tongue; then tie the nervous thread to the large part, until the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is hardness or numbness, and it's due to a sudden wound, then apply the poultice and tie that bond; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is below; and when you are done, lift up the liquid rose and easy water, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen tent; and keep the patient in this way every night, so that the wound cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bloody discharge comes forth, then place it on the glassy surface and broil it; and if the blood spreads, then cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it as being of fusse color or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining into blenchor, and there is moisture, then put in a compress, and make a small poultice, and deliver from one side to the other; and if the blood increases at your work, put vitriol powder on top until it is stopped, then return to your work until you have done everything right; then lift up the rosewater and vinegar mixture, and cure with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes a swelling comes within the throat called "godath", and one properly calls them "glanders", and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, beware: if it is an abscess of small sense and fusiform color, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch with iron, also because of the bloody discharge; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will cut it out, or it would break apart by itself; and if it is a whitish color, and the root is subtle, prepare your instrument to cut, but first make sure that the abscess has calmed down and is appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sit the patient before the sun, and his limbs be in their natural state, and the work be done on the mouth and the servant take hold of the tongue between his hands, and press the tongue downward to all the instrument, for this is its form; and it can be made of silver or subtle iron just like small knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take a compress and insert it into the almond, and draw it up above as far as you can; and draw nothing else with it, then bind at the instrument, so that it forms, which seems like one force; and yet the head is bent, and one side to another, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then bind it with pincers, so that it forms:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be torn from one side and the other; and when you have bound one of the almonds, then bind the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and hot and vinegar mixture, and if there is decoration of blood, gargle the patient with water or cooked grape pome husks, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses are born in the throat than the two almonds, so bind them then in this way as the two almonds are bound.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, namely the abscess of little sense; and I had well closed off all the throat, so that the woman could not expire because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she had remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced its way out through two holes of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Then I acted quickly and inserted one probe, then the discharge flowed, and there was a great deal of pus; then I reinserted the probe into the other nostril, and opened up the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I inserted the probe into this abscess, and cut out a part, and only a little blood flowed out; and thus the passage in the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing back, and filling up the space I had emptied, until it became very large; then I encircled and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained growing; and I departed from those parts, leaving God to do with them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it grows downward to the socket, and it is emptied and is long, so it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below large and rounded, then it is called "socket".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the boil or abscess is calmed down, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to cut; and that which is rounded and assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a rusty color or black, then it is necessary to avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, to have the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue onto the instrument which we have mentioned before; then insert the catheter into the socket, and guide it downward, and cut with the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the superfluity that is outside of natural bounds; for if you cover more, you will cause harm to voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of II almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about covering, then you must use cunning at the cauterization of the senses to dispel fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cauterization is hot and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts their head in your hand, and then presses their tongue to the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cauterization, and mixes with hot and living coal, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in using the handle of this instrument, in which is its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, not the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and put it in a place, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with hard earth, and inside the pot have one instrument shaved according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it is of silver or of copper, and one of the keys is inserted into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is deadened; afterwards it often resumes, until the eye dries, and be sure you do not do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things happen there; nor do this thing except at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a thread and put a quill of egg inside the head, so that the patient's mouth does not have too much heat; for the quill of egg does not allow the vapor to burden the mouth, and it is good care together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is applied to the throat or spine of a fish or any thing; so it is necessary that you try what you can see, and press the tongue on the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move; and what does not appear and is returned to the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit while the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing is purged through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of bread, or a lettuce root, or one piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, then swallow it; and when it comes up, it will be strained, and then you will pull out; and if it does not come up with what we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the head so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and have the head lifted upwards; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all life depart from it, nor push the bone inside; and it is better for the patient to insert the instrument, because then or the thing is purged; if they insert it downward, or pull it out slowly with all the instrument equal, until it is pulled out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the snot from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	The flesh is not healed, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not benefit, then look at the patient's throat to the sun, then press his tongue onto the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see sweat, so treat it with small needles or subtle forceps that are good for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a hair-thin cord and tie it around the patient's throat, then heat the point where the cord meets the skin with fire, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is bothered by water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full pitcher of cold water, and make the patient spit it out, and swallow it without gluttony, and move their mouth often with their hand; and as soon as the sweat feels the water, let them spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she does not spit as we said, then suffumigate the patient with asafetida at the instrument that I have described in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will clear without effort.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where it has live coals, and there is a cloth covered with a perforated sheet in the middle, and in that hole is the key of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the cane in their mouth, and closes their mouth, so that the smoke does not come out but reaches just to the sweat; and the sweat will now fall, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to pass through this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one pulls out the snot is like this: when it can be seen, it resembles curved forceps suitable for entering the throat; and it has a resemblance to a bird's beak, and has asperity of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and behold the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what is remembered here after one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and it's in two manners in which one is similar itself, and that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fatty part are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce, until the bowels are moist according to their completion; and if there are such as it is necessary to pierce when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, just like those abscesses which are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves them until they are rotten around, by chance if the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes a contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it is rotten, it will harm the principal member; or it is at the foundation, so one should pierce it when it is dead; and it is not necessary that you pierce a hard abscess without digestion being complete, except for that which is near the foundation, lest it spread inwardly and become a fistula; and then it cannot heal in a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of perforation of the abscess when it has died according to its completion, and that is when the pain has subsided, and the departures of fever, and the diminution of pain and redness, and of swelling and disquieting of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you perform the perforation or more depending on the location of the abscess, and where it appears to be; and the perforation should be long in the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints, and nerves, and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pleasure.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who suffer, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh that is hardening, then it is best to leave the puncture so that it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it beforehand, the body will be drained of venom from there, and will be full of much filth; and by chance, the lips and the underlying parts may become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that are pierced according to the breadth of the body, according as it is needed by the members.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions in small abscesses, small punctures; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where one must cut the skin and cover; when it has become as dry as rags and is no longer pulsating, then do as one does with babies: and if there are those that are split in three angles, and if there are those whose edges are cut like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses from angels; and if there are those where you make a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil who have not point of chief, if like aposteme soft superficial, it is necessary that you make perforations peacefully; and it is necessary when the apostemes are big, and they have gathered great bowe, and you make perforations, so do not pull out all the bowe in this hour, but pull out part of it; then stop the aposteme just until another day, then pull out nothing else from there; do that several times at your pleasure, until the bowe is completely gone; likewise if the patient has weak vitality, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the hopes tremble at times with the exit of the bowe, lest by chance the patient dies, and you do not take heed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, exercise great caution in this chapter, and when you have pierced your aposteme, if the wound appears, and look to see if the wound of the aposteme is small; and if it is a smooth incision, then try to place a tent made of linen or old cotton there; and if it is a large aposteme, and there are many holes, it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that they come together against each other; and if you have cut into the aposteme a part of skin, and you have wrapped it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or a compress made of linen without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs at your operation, then administer cold and easily flowing water, and moisten the cloth, and place it on the area bleeding many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, then administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said to be good in this book, and if it is in winter, and the abscess or aposteme is very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on wet tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the abscess is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then detach the aposteme and the pus and cure it, as it is necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses; and I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come from the head, and they are like the manners of those who are on threads, just as a tailor is with a spider's web, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some big and fat ones that have moisture like blisters; and if there are those that are hard and stony to cut into, and one is not afraid as long as the artery does not go against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the tailor is that you test all the instruments that are called "entromissoires", from which the form comes after, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, make a hole in it above the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape it without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it will return if you leave anything; then plunge cotton in Egyptian oil, if present; if not, in water and oil, and fill the wound, and let it be until the next day; and those who remain from night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then rewrap the cotton, just as before, on the second day and the third day, until you know well that it does not remain wet; then treat the wound with ointment in a suitable manner, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess does not grow fat, then cut it according to this form, from long; and remove your fingers, and scrape off all around, and put all your care in pulling away the cloth where it lies; and if the arteries make you feel contrary, do what I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same with the abscess if it is stony, and cutting and curing as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on top of the stony abscess and the moist one, if it is lighter, because they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or the one I saw on an old woman's head had no moisture, and those were the abscesses that I cut on an old woman's head; and I found the abscess just like a dry, rough, and white stone, and could not break it; and if someone had done anything to it, they would have made as much of a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	En others abscesses coming from the head, greater than those that come to the chief of children and roots of ears, let the opening be always at its most dependent place, so as to make the pus issue; and the wound to be cured as it is needed.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and are many, and are joined together one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own coat, just as the night and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the likenesses of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are malignant and do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Then, if you see one with a good disposition for touching, and it resembles the color of the body, and is quiet on all sides, and is not inflamed at the neck or artery or conduit, and is not too deep; then you must scrape it above, and cut away each part, and use the two lips of the knife to sew up, if you need it, just as we have said in abscesses of the head; and work slowly and carefully, making sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, nor be too hasty with the spatula, lest your hands slip and you do not see too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you lance the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, then put in the wound a vitriol poultice, or some powders that stop bleeding, and bind the wound; and leave it so that the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work, until you have completed it; and then look at your patient's wound to see if there are any small scrofulae, and cut them out and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, then it is not necessary for you to cut out that scrofula in its root, but bind it with a strong double thread and let it fall away without harm; then fill the wound with old Egyptian cotton dipped in oil, and then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, then there will be no remaining superfluity due to the greatness of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you understand how to cover the root of it and pull forward, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that retain superfluity, open there where it appears to be the most inflamed; and open as has been said before, depending on this, then you should apply poultices with ointment and similar things, so that what remains of corruption is corrupted; and when the wound is well cleansed, then apply a poultice to draw out the flesh until it is healed.
de squinance	of scabies
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and that is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have scabies, it is necessary that the incision of the throat called "epiglote" be opened; and one does not make aid by these means, because all the veins and the pomegranate of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pomegranate, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to escape the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it below three circles or four small incisions across, between the two circles or according to the size of the syphac wound, not in the cartilage; and this way is suitable for the section of the epiglottis so that there will be no flesh, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, so it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all the edge, then cuts the leather until it comes to the chin; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the suture, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein at the chin which jumps forth by the broken joint and by the lack of voice; and leaves the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound with care, and sew all around without leaving any cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Also it is said that one should not do this just yet until the throat is entirely swelled, and the patient is judged to be on the point of death, and the breath fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglote for that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and for this, the ancients command to leave the wound open until the malady of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they command to sew up the wound and cure it, until it is cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young lady take the knife, and she stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of the channels of the womb; and I was called to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and I saw well that she had not cut the vein nor conducted it far from the throat, and the veins were flowing freely through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed the wound, and cured her until she was healed; and nothing befell the young lady except that she lost her voice, and returned to her usual state; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of jasper, and it is very common in women; and there are two kinds: natural, and accidental; or if it is natural, it has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is in two manners, of which one is like fat tissue, and the other manner is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be worked on with force except in a small one, and prove and search all around: if you find it to be like fat tissue, and does not fit into any vessel, then cut it off, just as one cuts off fat, and treat it thoroughly, if there is any; and examine well, and cure it as needed, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of the fat
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are ours, of which I will say all similar things; and now it is necessary that I say the whole difference that is between us and exit.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is hot and feverish, holding fast until the ebullition has passed, and the corruption is completed; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the nout there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and contains within it the sap, which is its own bag and follows the color of the body, and begins also like a wasp, and becomes large; and are according to two likenesses, either fat or moist, and with many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the fat, that you examine and inquire first through all the instruments called "entrails", according to what its form will be or chapter which comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses from us is that you take or find the moistest part that you see in the abscess, and turn your two pincers back and forth until you know that the instruments have pierced the core, according to the size of the abscess; then extract the instrument, and be careful so that it does not jump forward.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	Se moistor corrans cort, that will color it have, so let it be done as I said of other abscesses;
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it stays nothing, then comes the news again many times; and if there is a little left, and blood grieves, then apply the wound with some corrosive powders, and hold the wound, and put hot soothing things on top of the abscess, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed; and if the news is great, then cut off two lips of the wound, and cure those who injure the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beats against you or another thing that is contrary to you, or if you hurry and apply the lead of vitriol powder, and let it be for two days or three, until the wound purrs, and rest the ebullition of blood; then return to cutting off what remains of the fat.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Behold the shapes of the twisted instruments, and they are of three kinds: great, medium, and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb"; and there are also of three kinds: great, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula; and they are like the needles with which one sews sorcery, and they are made of yellow citrine, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are most tested for blacksmithing purposes to encircle the curvatures of fistula; and they are of three kinds: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the ulcers are many and similar, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and also there are ulcers that have two shapes in three ways; and also there are ulcers that have three shapes, and are the same in three ways; and also there are ulcers that have two shapes, and a single shape only, and are the same in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are cutting, and some have only just cut on one side, from which we scrape the flesh, because it is not suitable to touch the vein or nerve; and among these are the alembics replying in bands, so that the patient does not become aware of the opening of abscesses; and they come in three ways: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them excessively except on charmed places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and in similar places; and sometimes one makes a very small instrument, resembling scrapers for fingernails, according to this form, with which we stop bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the place that heals with completeness of veins and arteries, and sometimes returns according to this great form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Breast swelling occurs in some men when they begin to decay, until it seems like a woman's breast; and remain swollen and puffy, and whoever wants to cure them, must do so according to this form from line .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and apply a medicinal paste to the wound, letting it set with flesh; then bring together the two lips of the wound at their edge, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast droops down, and is swollen due to its great size as in women, so cut it into two sections above, by two similar incisions; thereby one part will be attached to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from line .b. to line .g.; then scrape off the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about edge and powder, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not yet fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to excessive bleeding, then you must fill the wound with damp cotton soaked in corrosive oil; and let it stay until it has consumed what remains and the fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses on the hips
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the hips are types of hard scrofulas with ridges, and some of them contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the swelling that is in the abscess has gone down, then fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment as needed, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a similar kind to scrofulas, then do it as we have said in incisions for scrofulas, and if the wound swells, then apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
