Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is blocked and the skin above it is sewn shut, then many abscesses occur; and so too happens it with a vein that is swollen and an abscess; and if one knows thus when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep; and when you sense it in your arms, then you sense extreme strain; and when it is due to the vein, then it is reason to flee appearances; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is below the armpits and shoulders and at the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore to avoid the iron treatment, and also he who is at the head should avoid it, and in him who has a swollen artery, make an incision above the skin that is long; then open up the flesh as much as possible, and carefully detach the artery from the flesh, so that it is completely exposed; then insert a needle underneath, and have it pierce to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have shown you about the extraction of the two arteries which are in temples; then tie off the place that is between the two ligatures with an interrupter so that the blood that is there flows out, and release the abscess; then apply the remedy as I have instructed you for a wound, until the ligature falls off; then cure those things that pertain to ointment accordingly, until it is healthy; and if the abscess is due to the swelling of the vein, then you should keep your hand on what you can remove from the abscess to all the skin, then insert the needle underneath where you hold in your hand, and have it pierce and there be a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess as I have told you, or tie off one of the two parts with the two keys of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads will not come out, then insert another needle underneath all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and bind the threads in four places; then cut away the abscess until the superfluous blood flows out, then cut away the superfluity of the skin and leave what is bound; then put on a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, and apply remedies for tents and ointments until it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses on the knees
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like abscesses come from the artery and vein, abscesses on the knees come when they are fatigued or from too much heavy labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, and it happens more often in armpits and arms and in all places where there are joints, and that is a grievous abscess, and its color seems the color of the flesh, and it is in many dispositions without pain; and when one strains at it strongly, then the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but beneath the skin; and it can be seen from all sides, and does not move forward or backward, nor below or above, and he who is in joints should not be cut by iron: perhaps there would be contraction; and he who is on the head or on the forehead, makes the leather to split.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, one should hold it with forceps and cut to its root; and if it is large, one should suspend it with an onychine, and flay it, then remove the bone and assemble the wound to the seam, and cure it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of big boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul,
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I found XVIII onces weighing, and in the other VI ounces, and the work of incision is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of artemisia is white and moist and of subtle root; if it copes with spatula wide, and let the fire cautery be present.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when the cutter comes often too great losses of blood, and if the blood flows forth, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made linen thread, and tie the artemisia as we have said, and leave it for 2 days; and then restrain it, and do not cease restraining the linen thread until it consumes the artemisia, and choose by means of it what work is to be done; and if the roots are large, fear to cut them forth oneself because of the belly, but you may well cut off half, then cauterize so that it does not relapse; then cure the wound, and make sure you do not cut off the thulium which is of a flux color and poor sense and of little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess enchanced, and I will come to the treatment of chancres here after.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	Se the appearance of the wound comes from fire cautery or cutting of sycamore bark, and is above the belly and in some of the buttocks, as it happens in other wounds, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what precedes, or of pus; and if this is from the wound of sycamore bark and from the issue of the boil, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and appears with diverse issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press it at its sides it swells up, and then returns, and by chance it becomes hard, and greatly increases at the entrance of the bath and from great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it's because of moisture, it's a light thing, and appears well when you press it with your hand, not constraining at all; and if it's because of blood, then it appears by these signs: the abscess is large and hard, and has a quantity to it; and if it's because of pus, then it's soft to the touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is from the blood of an artery, or vein, or pus.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	You must leave the wound alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the abscess is due to the intestine or bowel, you should instruct the patient to hold his breath, and be straight as far as possible; then sign around the boil with your finger; then command him to sit quietly between your hands, then go around the area that you have signed all along the abdomen; then cut off half of the abscess above the great artery; then tie it around with a strong thread or cord firmly, and make sure the ligament is secure; then work on the remaining half of the abscess extended over the ligament, and put your index finger inside, and follow the intestine; if you find it caught by the ligament, release it, and push the intestine back into the abdomen; and if you find the bowel, take hold of it with the artery, and cut away the superfluity; and if the artery or vein resists, go gently around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads on them, and put the needles through what you have done in a cross shape as when you are piercing; then draw the abscess up to four fingers above the needles, and if you see something, remove the needles, and leave the area alone until it can heal, and cut away the dead flesh by yourself; or you may need to cut it when it is subtle and perishable, then cure what needs curing, and let the abscess be as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the wound as needed, and seal the wound.
dou chancre	of chancres
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the likenesses of chancres, and how one should work with medicines, and how one must avoid iron treatment; and we say that chancres are born in the womb, and great caution is needed in its cure, and the ancients say that when chancres are on the skin or in a place where it can be scratched like chancres which are in the armpits, and in the groin, and in similar places, one must completely remove it when it begins; and when it is great and old, then it is not necessary to approach it, for I have never seen anyone cured of it; nor has anyone been healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place or can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient with black coles once or twice; then make them healthy if they have manifest repletion; then dress the patient's wound well to do the work; then throw away your splints or chancres, and clean it from all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow fully, and press the wound gently with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding of blood makes you contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have spoken of the likenesses of dropsy in the division, and how the assembly of water is done, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by fire: it is lit up only; and one should not touch iron on these two likenesses: it's to say, tympanites and hypochondriasis, for it is mortal things; therefore when you medicate this likeness of dropsy which is called "eclites" from medicines, and the cure does not profit, then look if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease than dropsy, as today's diarrhea and similar things; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient with strong virtue, and he has no other disease than dropsy only, and he is not too old nor too young, then thus proceed: lift up the patient straight onto your hands, and the attendants press the belly outwardly pushing the water to the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spatula-like spine according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And it should be cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And it should be incised at a point, and yet not so deep that it can come all the way to the intestine when one inserts it in, and cannot hurt; then look if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if so, you must cut in above the lower jawbone three fingers on top of the little finger; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, then your incision should be on the left side of the lower jawbone three fingers; and if it's due to mucus, then it will be on the right side, and it does not matter that the patient lies above the incision so that the superfluities do not flow to that weak part; then pierce all the skin with this instrument, and plug it in, and lift your hand up to the whole spatula between the skin and the flesh just as when shearing at the size of an fingernail or about that; then pierce the flesh so that the spatula comes to the right place, and that is the vein's flow, then treat the water, and insert this instrument for which it is the shape.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it appears like a subtle silver chain, and is of earth or light archer's stone, and has in the part below one small perforation; and on the side from here, three perforations; and two on the other side, and one on another; and the head is shaped as if cut with a pen, and this is the form of the incision that writers shape the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top are the almighty ones, such that when instruments come to water, they now descend upon the instrument; then empty it, either half or a third part, for if you empty more than is needed at this hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit from the arm, or they fall facedown, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of their strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and their pulses; then draw the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now for the reason that stops the perforation which is above the syringe, of which I spoke, such that you pierce in this manner; then recommence the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw off a small quantity of water; do this some days, and take care not to overflow as long as there is still only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient, and leave him much water, so that he may be cured of sepulture or sandy earth, and by much sweating or bathing in the sun, and if he is instructed to drink; and the curing of drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterizing on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	None are born children who do not have a pustule on the penis, or the pustules are small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it seems necessary at once to pierce through all the skin very subtly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put the pustule in a small clove and tie it and keep it thus for three days or four, and when it wants to make urine, then remove the clove and let him urinate, and then replace it; and by chance there is no need, for the urine that comes out will not close it.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	That which belongs to the gout is small, so it is medicated with clove oil, as we have said, so that it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the gout in its place are blinded, because some people are born with the gout at the head of the penis, for which they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis high; and they cannot reproduce because the matter cannot come to the womb, and that is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on their back, and then the top of the penis is bent and cut like the shape of a pen nib, so that the hole opens in its place, as it should; and be careful not to disturb the blood that comes out many times, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops bleeding, and cure the wound until they are healed.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	These pustules often come on the penis, and it is a foul appearance; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; therefore, take them at one subtle poultice, and cut and clean all of them, then apply wet cotton in Egyptian ointment; then treat with divine ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of foul color and foul smell, then it is necessary for you to apply a cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it open, and the boil is on the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it is necessary for you to remove the boil that is inside first; and when it is closed, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car when you treat it together, the head of the penis is not assured that it will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come to its tip and in its sheath; so it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply the poultice of honey and flour made from pomegranate bark and vetch, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding comes forth, apply the lunar cauterization in this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterization is helpful in two dispositions together: that is to say, in bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you tie a linen cloth around the urethra and make the patient urinate between; and when the hairs are rough at the head of the penis which have not been circumcised, or due to injury or abscess, it is necessary then that you remove it with a sharp instrument, so that the ligament is loosened, and the head of the penis be freed from all parts; and if this is a troublesome thing to discuss, it is necessary that you remove it with a spatula-like instrument somewhat below the head of the penis and the skin; then wash it gently between two and put a thin damp cloth of linen in cold water, so that it does not become rough again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the severing of continuity like other wounds; however, when we do this work by our own desire and properly for children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the most gentle for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the greatest part of masters and seniors who performed circumcision around one inch, and with forces, and all a new needle; it would be cut because there are two layers, and by chance if you cut above and leave that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is to cut again, and there is double pain, and at the purification which is above the skin is not assuredly secure the point of the member; and at the purification of the wound by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times it happens thus that they have no need for purification and I want this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is made with force, I have found the goodness of experience, for the forces cut equally well above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car when you press your hand, so it cuts evenly in all the tautness; but let the thread be well stretched around the leather; and be the manner of the first work such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are not making him bind the thread around the shaft for more than just a little, and then make it relax in all the ways you can; then make it rest between your hands straight up, and repeat the forces between your hands or below your feet so the child does not see it, nor any of the tools; then put your hand on the shaft and blow or breathe, and train it to go up as far as the head of the shaft is; then clean it well of the filth that has assembled there, then tie a knot with a double thread, then tie below one link to another link; and hold it by both ends through the second loop at the pouch and the left index finger, and compress between the two links, then lift the breath above hastily and pull the head of the shaft; then let blood flow little by little, for this is what mothers do; and put powder on top and on top of the powder, a cloth glued to an egg white cooked without water, mixed with good rose oil and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for purification is this: two fingers should be held and should be pressing, and they should be equal to the width of a thumb.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purification is when the blood flows into the incision; therefore it is necessary that you stretch it to your finger, so that the lump makes an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot keep it at your finger, then hold with forceps, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it exceeds three days, and what is below the penis is swollen, then leave it until the abscess is appeased, and lightly scrape; then cut as you can move, and be careful of the part of the penis, for it will harm nothing.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the wound with soothing powder, as we have said to treat powders, and if you cut too much from the skin, and it goes above, it will harm nothing; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Li retenue of the urine is caused by obstruction of stone, or congealed blood, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is stuck or lodged at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees; and let his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from above the back, and restrain the patient's abdomen as much as he can; and then constrain the neck of the bladder to express itself through the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come forth, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction using all the instruments which are called "siringue", and this is its form: and it should be made of subtle silver hair, like a bird's feather; and the cord should be one palm and a half long, and very fine at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et the manner of the issue of the urine is that you take a double thread and tie it to the top of a piece of wool or cotton, and put the top of the thread inside the syringe; and remove the superfluous wool and put it just up to the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a siege, and raise the bladder and the urine tube with moist and olive oil and dry water; then put the syringe lightly into the urine tube as far as it comes to the root of the tube, then double the tube upwards towards the mouth; then put the syringe forward just to the bladder, and let the patient come just to the empty thing, and that is not done according to this order unless because the guide or what goes in her is twisted; then remove the thread from all the wool and cotton, and the urine follows the wool, then strain it out, and make the urine flow again; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When bleedings or blood comes into the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled there, and you see it dripping with waters and medicines, then do with all the instrument that is called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	Elle is closed, and if it has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the wick is trimmed so that the medicine can flow well without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see your medicines going into the bladder, put the top of the syringe in the moisture, and pull on the pulling string which is inside; then pull the moisture into the syringe, and then push hard on the string inside; then the moisture will enter and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of subtle enema by which one enemas the bladder: thus it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or archaic, and the head is higher; and below, one side or the cord falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture that you see enemas the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the pessary on the fire; then push the top of the syringe into the vagina, then strain your hand on the bladder until all the moisture is released, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then push the thread firmly into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dale, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do so with your hand as you did with the bladder, pressing until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone and extraction together with medicines; and I said the difference between the stoned abscesses as regards rains, and all signs, and which kind of stone one should work on; and in the bladder, and in the sheath; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is stoned in the bladder happens more often to children, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and it appears hare-like, and the patient's sheath swells, and he pees many times, and then becomes inflamed; and many of these stones are formed at the foundations; and it is lighter to heal children until they are three years old, and it is much more grievous in old men, and it is moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those with a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with laxatives, in order to draw out all the bile that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders searching for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take hold of the patient by the feet, and throw him backwards and move him down below, so that the stone descends to the very bottom of the bladder, and sometimes may fall from a great height; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely tilted downwards; then search and touch inside; if you feel the stone in position, then hasten now to cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall when touched entirely, moisten your left index finger with oil from your left hand if the patient is a youth, or your middle finger if the patient is an adult; and insert it into his fundament, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, then press it onto the neck of the bladder; then press up on your finger, and push it out behind where you see fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the skin above in height, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the skin on the part where one makes the incision; then put in the spatula copant, which is this form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between those who are between the testicles and the fundament, not at all in the middle but at the side of the left naively; and be straight on the stone, and your two feet should be against the fundament, and be the cut of the traversing if it is wide enough to push forward, and inwardly narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not at all too great; by chance the pressure so the foot that is on the fundament, that it jumps away without effort; and know that there are stones where there are angles, and edges: then it is hard to get out; and there are those which are hollow, similar to a gourd, and rounded, whose exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And to those stones where there are angles and edges, make the cut more great; and if it does not jump, then it is necessary that you stretch over the pliers which are like a file at the head, in order to strain the stone so that it does not escape; or you put underneath the instrument curved at the head; and if you cannot bend it thus, then widen the hole and if the flesh falls off, then bind with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, then butt first the largest against the neck of the bladder, then cut on top, then pull out further, and the small ones afterwards if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if she is very large, then it must be cut out, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out soon because the wound cannot heal; but always try to drain, or to extract with pincers, as much as you can pull it apart by pieces; and when you have completed your work, then fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put a damp cloth on top of oil and wine, or on oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the hot abscess; then turn the patient over onto his back, and do not remove the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, then raise the patient very well with oil and water, and then cure him with diaphrenic ointment and basilicon ointment, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if the abscess becomes hot and boils in the wound, and coagulated blood forms in the bladder, and is retained by it, which prevents the urine from flowing with its usual rhythm: then open up the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and destroy it; then wash the wound with water, vinegar, and soap, and help him in all the ways you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the operations you perform on him, that you bind his two hips together, and assemble the medicines on his bed.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethral canal of the penis, and fixed inside, and the urine cannot come out; so do what I say, that you cut many times, or excuse yourself from cutting because of this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod according to this form and be fixed at three angles in one handle:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and wrap it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot go further into the bladder; then push the forceps into the penis gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the forceps slowly in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then the urine will come out soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then it is broken and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this because of anything that hinders it, then tie one thread below the stone and another above, then bend the penis around the stone between the two threads, then pull it out and loosen the string, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There often happens that the stone is inserted in women, and if it ever does, it is a grievous cure, and is defended by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who reveals herself to midwives, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; and the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing this art of hands;
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to below, so that it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, there where it is most apparent, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move your hand above or below the stone, and make the first incision small; then put the ruler in the incision if you sense the stone so far into the wound that the stone can come out freely, and know that many types of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and rounded, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the likenesses to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood veins, then put white vinegar broth at the site, and hold it there for an hour until the blood is staunched; then return to your work, as long as the stone is out, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to aid you in your work; and if the blood veins, and this is due to the artery that has been cut, then put powder on the site and strain through tents and cloth, and do not start again with this, and leave the stone alone and do not pull it out, for fear the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the place is clean, then come back to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshly hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramica aquosa is nothing else than a gathering of moisture or white fluid, which is beneath the skin of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "syphac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, as if it were another egg; and it's the skin of the testicle between the white syphac that we have said; and this does not happen unless one is not.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramica is due to weakness that comes from the testicles, and it spreads that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the groin, and this moisture has many colors: or it's declining to yellow, or without red, or black, or white as water, and it happens often; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is a whitish scab as we said, then it's the abscess responding, I will not be long like the shape of an egg, and does not open the groin, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture on the proper cloth, then it's the abscess responding with part of the egg, and because of this one thinks it's another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the groin and the whitish scab, one feels well; therefore when you see the color of the moisture, try to experience all the surrounding quadrature, for which the shape is as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what comes after the surrounding quadrature, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et when we cure it with iron, so the patient must be strengthened according to their power and the replenishment of their body; then bind them on their back on something slightly high, and place a great many cloths under them; then sit on their left side, and instruct the attendant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two rib bones of the kidney; then take the spatula lying nearby, and cut the skin of the kidneys between the long and the short, until it reaches the nail, and make your incision entirely straight as you cut through the skin of the kidneys up to where it becomes white, and scrape out the fat subtlety according to their power; then pierce the white part with water into a large perforation, and extract all the water, and then place one's fingers on top; and do not touch the kidney but only the white part; cut the entire or in pieces similarly the edge of it subtly, so that if you do not cut well, the water will return; and if the urine jumps out at your work, then bind it back to its place when you have completed the work on the skin; then assemble the two halves of the kidney's rib bones with a seam, and cure it as with other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you lift up the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the corruption of blood; then cut off the testicle to all the suspended part, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the swelling is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two threads; so cut the other part as you have done the first one equally, then stop the bleeding, and put a moist cloth on the wound soaked in rose oil; and put another moist cloth in wine and oil, and put it above both bones, and put above double cloths, and tie everything together with all the threads that are according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and put them in wool according to this appearance, and be assembled by sewing in the belt of the braies, and one of the keys takes on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the finger; and the other two heads above the two angles, and be all assembled into a restraint in the buckle of the braier; and sometimes this thread is medicine for the cautery instead of iron cutting, and it is that you take one cautery cultural subtle, and cut the skin of the bones, and be heated as we have said, so that the white scab that contains the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that scab at intervals, and scrape off with a hot subtle cautery:

And the cauterized area in all ways that you can, until you have reached everything; and be sure that the fire does not touch the yolk; and know that this work is more safe; and be careful of dismemberment of blood, and more so of the works of cutting; and if nothing makes you contrary, or abscess or dismemberment of blood or other thing, take care of what makes you contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to endure this work because of its horrible nature, then perforation should be performed, as I am telling you, and it is that when you are well assured by the signs we have said that a poultice is good, make the patient sit on a light siege; then pierce the abscess in the lower part of the entire spacious area, and make the perforation long along the length of the body; and let the wound be wide so that all the water can flow forth; then put cotton on the site, bind it, and let the remaining water drain forth, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow water to issue from the mouth of the wound, it is necessary for you to insert a needle or instrument used for draining the fluid of dropsies, by which the form is as before; and enlarge the poultice on the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or so around, and when it is assembled as before, and thus will the patient pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the cones
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this treatise there are many fears and dispositions, which seems to me that much is gained by leaving it as it is; and I will tell you the work and similar things about the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and even to the cones; and this is by much chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known by excessive bitter and ague, which spreads to the groin, or through percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the flesh; and it does not find pain, and is a grievous abscess; and perhaps there are some grievous abscesses that are pus-filled and stone-like, with a foul color, and sometimes comes from the back of an artery, or from swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from the back of an artery, it is known by the hot disposition of abscess, when you press it at your elbow; and it does not behoove that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Cil who is made of vein swelling is known by its disposition to the expression of finger touching, and can well perform the procedure on this similarity, and on other limbs; and that you make a cut in the key of knuckles, then lift the yolk up high, and tie it with white silk thread, and deliver the suspensory all around the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the yolk is already swollen with these veins, then it's necessary that you tie the yolk and make a cut; and if it's air-filled or inside the vessels, then it's necessary that you deliver all that tension and make another cut.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the vein is in the lower part, then it is necessary that you cut it all, and draw out the yolk, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, then dress the wound with damp wool cloth in rose oil and wine, and care for it with other cares until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the cones
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping similar to a berry, with the softening of knuckles, and the patient's pain increases when it moves; and the treatment for this disease is just as frightening as the previous one, and although we will tell you how to do it according to what the old people did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.
