Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "beef sickness", because it often affects oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and one feels it well as it moves from member to member, until it pierces the skin where it is going, and jumps out; and it is filled with the putridity of some humors, such as worms, serpents, lice, and ascarides in the belly; and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance it returns, and destroys the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healing and moving, there is no one who can do anything except when it moves: so then you must tie the above and below with a strong string tightly, then cut on top and draw it forth, and if the vein is pierced deeply in the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire above until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does, it runs to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the chief part of the eye, then bind strongly below it a small circle, then cut on top, and draw it forth; and one must use the patient with purifying medicines soluble for bad humors produced, and beware of meats that produce corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and can move from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and I probed afterwards, the sight ascended as much as a worm on the shoulder, sooner than anything, like very white silver when it cuts from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then a little afterwards ran throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me it was rotating around the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved thus from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had thought that it would be good for the pain to move from one place to another, but I did not want it to, just as I saw in the woman; and I thought to myself that it was because the woman's body is too dry, and her veins are uncovered, and therefore that constraint appears; and do not pay attention according to this reason to those who have moist bodies and veins that respond.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, then bind above and below hastily, and then cut above until the ventosities are forced to come out; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it in your eyes, then treat with those who calm ventosities, such as fetid pills and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their kinds is that there are those with large points, small ones, hooked ones, and soldered ones; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that falls in any member falls in two ways: either it falls in the principal limb, such as head, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you hereafter, warns you: so it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not warn you, and the arrow is not at all gone deep, then heal it, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and jumps over the skull which is above the brain, is when there is numbness and darkness and distortion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes this happens without fever of nose or ears; and sometimes it affects speech and voice; and a white moist pustule jumps out like boils, and also as if burned by fire; and if this sign warns you, then take care of the cure, and extract the arrow if it is not too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it strikes the heart is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the arrow also moves like the hairs, and with cold black blood, and comes with chilliness and cold sweat, and faintness: know then without doubt that death ensues.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow when the kidney is hit is that without any foam it bursts forth from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's color changes, and sighs deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes in the covering of the breastbone, it is near the little ribs; and vomits a great deal of yellow bile and great pain and sighs; and all the members of the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow strikes the stomach by chance, so that something from the undigested meat falls out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow strikes the belly, and a piece of bowstring jumps out through the intestines without any hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow strikes the bladder, and urine jumps out and flows forth, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and shoulders and throat and shoulder blade and armrest and spine of the back and forehead and hips and thighs and legs, and a similar limb, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one man that an arrow struck him in the armpit at the root of the neck; I tried it and pulled it out from the other side under the fatty part of the ear, and he was healed without injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that had struck him in the fatty part of the eye under the eyebrow bone, and the arrow was bent back, and could not be extracted except for the point next to where it was, and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow, so that anyone could see it without needing to look closely; the game was healed, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And extract an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab to the ears: I saw the bearded ones, and refined it so much that I drew it out, and the Christian became well.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And extract an arrow from the man, which was stuck in his belly, and I thought he would die; and then after XXX days, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, and guided it, and drew it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if the arrow falls on the back of a man, and the wound is sewn up above; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change his natural dispositions, nor finds harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and it remained thus without suffering great pain; and many similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow wound in the man of the princes the king, which had been shot into his left side, and was slightly declining to the right part; and the arrow was entirely covered. I was called to the treatment after it had been shot three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched for it with all subtlety and didn't find it; and he felt puncturing and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I placed on the wound a plaster attracting and digestive, because the swelling didn't develop; and the swelling of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I placed the plaster many days, and the wound healed above, and the patient remained thus for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day within his flesh; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied medicine with corrosive properties to the wound by hand for several days, until it was open, and I tried it, and felt the tip of the arrowhead which had been embedded at the site; then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that medicine, so that the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and it did well beyond 4 months, and then healed to such a point that I put in forceps, and manipulated it from one side and the other, and could not come out; then I did not stop subtlety and ingenuity with instruments, until I took out the wound well done, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I held on and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the surgeon judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was entirely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or it is said the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, for books cannot contain everything; but wise and experienced masters can well enough grasp a small matter, and on what is present and failing, find new work and nine instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not arise from members where they are inserted except by two manners: or by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which jumps out on the other side is an entering arrow into flesh, and sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump out now, so let it stay until the flesh is around it, and the issue is alleviated; and likewise if it's inserted in bone, and can't come out, so leave it thus for some days, and gently move each day; and then it jumps out, and if it doesn't, so make a small incision all around, until the skin around it is stretched, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	Et if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the vents of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said happen to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it becomes equal after a few days, because if the arrow comes close to the skull, it's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come close to the skull, and the patient remains some days without bad accident, then the doctor should guide the extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck and cannot come out further, then administer theriacs around, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the body so that it cannot be seen, search for it throughout the tent; and if you find it, extract it with some suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, cut away until the wound is large; and extract the arrow if you can, and if it has ears where it holds fast, remove the flesh that is stuck for two parts as far as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, so that you can pull it out; and be subtle in not breaking the arrow, lest you would draw it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the next day and pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you contrary, then follow what we said in its chapter about treatment; and beware of incising the nerve and vein, and make a plan how to draw out the arrow without danger, whether soon or late, firmly or gently; and put the patient as he was when the arrow hit him, for it is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot, then do according to what the sign shows.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another side, or if it shows something from there, or the skin is swollen in such a place as to be seen or felt uncomfortably: cut then above, until forceps can take hold, and then pull out: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, as far as it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it and start the extraction again until it comes out: and if there is pus from the arrow, then cover all of it; and if the pus bursts forth, and you must administer treatment, then provide an instrument with a toothed edge, so that the point of the arrow goes into the teeth of the instrument; and then push forward, and if the arrow is extracted, then insert the instrument with its toothed edge entering inside to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, then it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as is proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow strikes or pierces the belly or bladder or ribcage, and it is nearby, and you can cut on it, then do so; and take care not to cut the vein or nerve, and then pull it out, and then dress the wound as necessary; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one treats arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and look at this form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, small, and petty, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the hair's tip is also like the feather of a bird, to push against the point of the arrow, as follows:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for pushing and for extracting is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one cures oneself, of which there are 16 on the head, to wit: two beats that are after the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that appear in the two temples; and two veins that are in the two eyelids of both eyes, which are called "aspirés"; and one vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and one vein that is on the crown of the head; and the two grooves that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips below the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used for bleeding are two in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side, and people call it "the chief's vein"; and the median vein, which is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and people call it "the heart's vein"; and the basilic vein is on the right side, and people call it "the belly's vein"; and it lies above the elbow, and it is that one used for bleeding, which appears manifestly above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the wrist and ankle veins, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the fold of the armpit on the left side, and the second is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse" which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indicative, and boute la lancette desoz, and lieve la voine en haut, and la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, and faire corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, and met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; and then la lie forment, and la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; and nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding from the vein of the forehead is as valuable as the bleeding from the cephalic vein in old-fashioned maladies of the face, and in migraine, and in redness; and the qualities are such that the patient strains his neck while twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or other thing, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is sound and not once an hour with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not necessary that the opening be too wide; and the wound to cross, because the bone is pressed, and by chance break the opening when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding from the two veins that are in both arm-pits is helpful to those with fever, and with tinea, and with redness, and with greenish-yellow discharge in the eye, and with maladies of the face; and the qualities of their bleeding are such that the patient strains his neck while twisting by any ligament, just as before; then let it bleed, and be the blood of the travers, a bit long, a bit wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the opening is subtle, by chance it will break; then make an incision of blood, until you have need of it, and then bind on cotton, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the neck vein is so valuable that it can cure a fever, and a sudden fright, and facial diseases such as migraine and flush that comes to the face, and indeed when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient will tighten his throat, then restrain his neck to his left hand, and take a long thin flame, and place it between the upper lip and the nostrils, for the vein does not open well in this way, and the blood will start flowing now, do not go too deep into the fontanelle, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it at night, for it is very quickly restored; and that is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two jugular veins helps with the constriction of the arteries, and the beginning of menstruation, and many diseases, and epilepsy, and corrosion, and herpes, and ulcers; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens his throat below one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be sitting on the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a stool, then open the long vein a little widely, then take the blood temperamentally, or as much as is necessary; then do the other side in the other vein, then release the tie, and constrict the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the healing of books
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The vein of the upper lips is helpful to purging in the mouth, and to corrupting of gums, and breaking of lips, and around the navel.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the healing is to make the patient sit before you, and strain his neck as I said; then turn the book, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being black, and by having small black lines around them: cut then one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, then cut the larger one from each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the healing beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The healing beneath the tongue is helpful after the cephalic healing, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the healer is that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and lifts up their tongue, and looks under each side one black vein: heal then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly used for bleeding are treated in two ways: either by pricking them with a large flinty mirtin, or an olive-colored subtle one as cutters trench, and it is called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the wide opening is well-known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the neck veins that are full of thick blood visible on the surface, and which contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive-colored flint.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle and pointed, and is for bleeding the subtle veins, or where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the stomach; and it is necessary for the physician to bleed properly, and to be careful of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if the artery is cut and blood flows out, it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and one should not prick the flame, but rather incise it like anesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then you should manipulate it, and change to another one; or you want some rain from it, or you bleed in its place in the arm: it opens manifestly; and the cupping glass anesil is empty, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you manipulate the arm, touching the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with an ink, and bind the arm, and cup the vein of the empty glass; and beware that you do not strike at the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it flowing up high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood from the artery: hasten then, and place your elbow long, then take away your elbow if the bleeding subsides, as often happens; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and be on guard, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not ceased, and it complains to you, and the remedy is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head of it retires; and cease the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of fig skin, and cut it, and take one half and tie it well just above the other day; if the bleeding stops, that's good; if not, then cure it with powders that stop blood, as we have said, for the smallness of the wound and the power of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the vein is so helpful that it treats blood from above the head and below the body, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the surgeon to beware of the nerve that is below, and if he pierces too deep and finds the nerve, and it swells and the bleeding is hindered, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men due to its subtlety, then you must stop the bleeding with anesthetics; and hide the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is vein between the two nerves, then cut the long piece.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the cephalic [region] so helps that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to let blood flow into the olivary or myrtle flame, for it is the most saving of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place and not cause any harm if one has to start over the first time, and then begin again; and in some cases, the places swell in certain men, when one starts over the first time, but does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is necessary only to preserve health and to prevent diseases from coming; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins that are said to be good: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of autumn or winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one should bleed on the first day or third day after the second hour or third part of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The wound physician who tends to illnesses has no fixed schedule, but rather when need arises by day or night, at all hours and in all times; and it is not necessary to treat children until they are fourteen years old, nor women who are nursing except for the first quarter of a month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one bleed elderly people who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to heal, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary for them to purge their intestines with a gentle enema, if they have many bad humors retained, so that the veins do not absorb superfluous fluids which are harmful to the main members; nor does one recover from illness who is too filled with meat, or drunk, as long as they remain so, nor those afflicted with dropsy; and beware of healing after a colic passion, vomiting, and abdominal decoration, and frequent visits to a woman, labor, watching, and fasting, and all that is contrary to nature, or by the arm or body; then subtlety the humors if the blood is thick, through foods, drinks, and medicines, as long as you have the power; then enter into a bath, unless something prevents it, in order to subtletize the blood, and heal from the opening of the stomach around the third hour, as we have said; and guard that day from labor, pain, luxury, and similar things; and be merry and joyful, and let the healer be higher than the one who is being healed, and rub the arm twice or three times, then loosen the ligament above gently, for when it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow properly; and then rub the area with both hands, until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the healer's thumb with a little old oil, and place their left hand on that vein below the navel, about a finger-width from where they want to heal, so that the vein does not fail and collapse when it is cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Car there are veins that flow like strings to the surgeon, and those that are full of windiness, so that when you place the flame on them, they retreat from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with these; and if you open the vein, the wound will be too narrow, therefore it is necessary for the surgeons to be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens at first time, that is good; if not, then it starts again a little below or above quickly, as long as the swelling is not present.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is puffed up, and the patient is frightened, let him rest for a day or two, and do not bind his arm: by chance an abscess will form; don't enter into the bath, then resume the treatment if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, or the bleeding is subtle, and you doubt that there won't be as much blood as you see, then trust in that same wound itself to let out all the flame properly; and work quickly, while the swelling is puffed up; for this has happened many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb swollen, then do not resume bleeding, and put a little bit of linseed oil on it, because it lightens the body's blood, and makes the wound that the oil touches; and thus administer the linseed oil to each bleeding vein that you stop the veins, in order to stop the flow of blood; and this same thing works for triple and double wounds, when one puts it on the limb; then subtlety seeps out and spreads quickly when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not fully drained except at that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hasten and put a moist sponge on the limb in warm water and a little hot vinegar, and hold it for an hour; and you should do this after the bleeding stops from the vein, and if it remains on the limb after some days with any blackness or greenish color, then it will not harm him; and if you see fit, put some aloes or myrrh mixed in a calenture, mustard, or similar substance.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance at the wound of the basilica; then place your hand on it, and if you find the swelling soft to the pressure of the hand, that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not apply anything of what we have said, for by chance it may cause constriction of the artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the swelling, then treat with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each of the blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for him who is weak and alone, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and have the flaps be large; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and have him recover slowly and often, and one should have him recover by cutting across, not piercing; and this manner of recovery is saved from corruption of blood and numbness of nerve, and is worth more than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body is in need of bloodletting, it is necessary to give him moist bread soaked in grated apple juice; if he is overheated, then treat the wound three or four times with blood; and if he has a cold complexion, then soften the bread before bloodletting in a sweetened syrup, or in a perfumed honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it palms to the sinew, after the issue of much blood, then it is necessary that he drinks a broth of meat, and a subtle scented syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bend his arm and heal another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to bend his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he heals in seven hours after the first bleeding, or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wants to heal from another side, then he must heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood inside the body that is already heated up and causes fever; therefore, it is necessary to draw out a great quantity and widen the incision as long as it seems possible; then you should reward all the conditions of sinew, and place your hand on the pulses when it is healing, so that death does not come in place of pustules, and this happens many times when the physicians are negligent; and do not think that when you see the arm loosened, and blood issuing for the second time, and the incision is closed, that you should press strongly on it; nor if it is crooked, should you stretch out the arm quickly, for that would be bad; but leave it as long as it heals for the second time; or you will point to the tip of the flame, as long as the blood that is congealed at the incision of the vein issues forth, and place a small amount of oil on it, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then leave it alone and do not bind it tightly, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires bleeding a second time, then let the blood flow in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins on the arm are healed at the place of the main vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	Et the manner of the surgery is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the skin is red; then it is tied moderately, so that the vein appears well, and the blood is now let out through the small hole, not the wide one or the long one; and the pores are large, and the surgeon makes sure to clean well near the joint of the hand, and if nothing can come out, he puts the hand back in hot water, and lets the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if this is in summer, then do not put the hand back in hot water, for it is put more at risk than in winter; and the surgery of this vein is safer than all other veins, because there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The surgery of the abscess on the right hand is worth all diseases of the liver; and this is the method: strain the hand, and put it in hot water until the vein is empty, so that you can see it; and if the blood flows through, and you cut around it completely, then nothing will hurt; and don't go too far down into the wound, because the nerves are underneath all denuded of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound and can't come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as much as needed, put oil and silk on the vein to cauterize quickly, and thus do for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of the left hand is worth to the disease of the mouse, and do the same as I told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the spleen is worth to all diseases that are under the body, so much as diseases of the kidneys, and retention of fluids, and disease of the bladder, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its sickness is that the patient bathes his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein as long as it flows, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot they go out a great deal of urine; then she (the physician) gives or makes wider the vein, or at the ankle, which is more valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you make it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and the vein should go across as in cutting; and let there be no inflammation.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot back in water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the physician fails the first time, she renews it the second above a little bit, because the place is salty; nor should you doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make of the spleen of the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the thigh, and its vein is worth for the pain in the hip when it is full of blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	Et the qualities of his health are that the patient enters into the bath, and stretches above the ankle four times by twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then let the wound be treated in all ways you can, and crossing; and worth more than you cover it, for the limb is sound, and it is much returned to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not heal it, then let the wound be treated with some wine of that which opens the vein on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and take care of the nerves; and do so much good to the blood as you see, and then release the bandage, and put on cotton and bind it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Wounds from cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by making an incision and drawing blood, or without making an incision.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is without harming if it is done in two ways: either all at once or without hurting; and the cupping that is done by hurting and extracting blood is done in 14 places of the body, from which some are on top of the head; others are around the neck; and 2 others are on each side of the neck; and the one under the chin; and the one on both shoulders; and the one above the hips; and the ones on both arms; and the ones on both legs; and the ones on both ankles; and cupping does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore one should not weaken it at all, as is done with wound treatment; and it is not necessary to administer it, nor all at once nor without hurting, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessity demands ventosers due to diseases, or for the sake of customs, we shall administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between; because there are those who, when they need ventosers, have a heavy head; and there are those who experience repletion and redness on their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are those who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and have the tongue shrunk, and drink blood; and there are those who dream, and see through nocturnal blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command them to cup after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sweating of the head is a help to headache relief that comes into eyes, and it does not need to be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventosation is in place of the cephalic remedy, and it does not need to be used by those who are of cold complexion or have catharrhe, for it causes them great harm; and therefore, it is not suitable for old people nor those with cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are often cured with this method will become forgetful, and because of this it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The hiccoughs in the middle of the neck are located near the throat and the basilica, and for this reason they are valuable for the constriction of the chest, and for the splitting of the canal of the peritoneum, and for all, and for repletion; and it is necessary to be careful, because if she holds too tightly, she will injure the obliqueness or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The hiccoughs are also in the two armpits of the neck, and they are valuable for the pains of the head, and obtalmia and emigration, and for strangulation, and for the pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is located near the sanctuary of the basilica; and you should command the patient to express his hand when placing it, so that he does not pinch the artery, and does not cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The hiccoughs under the chin if they are worth a disease of the mouth, and corruption of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the cures of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The hiccoughs of the shoulders are worth a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The hiccoughs of the armpits are as valuable as the three veins of the arm, for it drains blood from these large veins; and command the patient not to strike too deeply within, for the place is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The hemorrhoids that are on the backside are worth hemorrhoids of the fundament, and diseases below, and it is necessary that the hemorrhoid be large, and be of earth, so it has need to well draw out; and by chance, if they were subtle, they would break; and there would be great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The hemorrhoids of the legs are clearly healed, for they bring forth blood from all the body, and are worth the ancient pains of the kidneys, bladder, and urinary tract, and restore the flowers; and they are in the place of the two shins, and two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause to come forth pus in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the poultice is that you put it on first empty, and then succeed in a timely way, and apply it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease to do so until you see the place red and swollen, and behold the bleeding of blood; then cut, and remove the poultices, and take heed to the condition of the body, for there are some who have hard flesh, and clear pores: thus it is necessary to wound only once, and necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then it is necessary to wound twice: the first time to subtlety the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, then it is necessary to wound a third time; and when we wish to draw out the blood little by little, then we should be satisfied only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a great deal of blood, so we repeat often; and if the blood is thick, so we pierce it deeply, and the ends should be cut so that the veins are felt suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have hard skin and strong pores that you anoint the sites of the cupping glasses with oil that is opening and dissolving: if this is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if this is in winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, then take bitter oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person has a tender skin and large pores, there is no need to put oil on it, but it is necessary to wash after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin seed water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, should wash with ease, or with myrtle water, and sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.
