And if the wound is near the shoulder's head, it is necessary that you put the ligature midway under the armpit, and the other towards the point of the shoulder, below the wound; and also if the wound is on the side of the point, it is necessary to put the ligature lightly, without labor, until the wound is even with the shoulder's head, and on the point; then set the wound straight, as needed, and bind it, lest apostemes come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if warm abscesses come, do not bind it at all until seven days, and put on a damp linen cloth in oil and rosewater, until the warm abscess is calmed; then bind it, and the manner of binding is that you put the poultice on the breakage, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and apply the compress, and bind on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in a position to be straightened without being hindered by anything, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use strait bands, and put on the breakage a band wider and stronger than the others, with two or three fingerbreadths between each band, and have each band so large that it passes over the breakage three fingers from each side; then bind on the bands, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the breakage, stronger and less strait.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of stars and estranging, as we have said, in the work that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is hot, let it bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days to the bandage, lest pruritus or inflammation come to the place, or the swelling not be able to come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is addressed, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident comes to it, then do not remove the bandage for more than three days or longer, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder one cushion plain of wool evenly, and look every hour throughout the day or night that the shape of the broken member does not move or become soft the ligaments; then address it by the power of medicine, and give him food as we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is for the first subtle ones; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be set in place for forty days from then; and then one must loosen and administer bath and medicinal ointments to direct the joint.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and swollen, it will remain for seven days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", where one is small and is the one that supports the pouch; and the other is large, and is the one that is below, towards the little thumb; by chance, it breaks the large foscile alone, or the small, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small bones are broken, restoration is easy and healing occurs; and when large bones are broken, healing is poor and more grievous than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it's the small bones that are broken alone, then one must gently stretch and set them equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it's the large bones that are broken, then one must stretch them more strongly; and extend on the first cushion, and lift the little pouch of the hand higher than the others, and let the small bones be lower than the other bones, and have the patient cross himself over himself, with the first cushion in front of him higher than the patient does not suffer any labor. Then stretch the attendants' arm to the part under his hand, or to the strap, and another attendant on the top.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mirror equal to his better form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are pieces, then set each one in its place, and if any are loose that can be pulled out, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a new one and use the bone, as we said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if you have spoken of the break with a wound in a singular chapter, then take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the treatment some abscesses arise, then make a paste of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and apply the paste subtly above, until the abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the wax, and put the poultice of miller's powder with a great deal of egg, and set the splints, and let the splint be on the breakage in this way: more strong and larger than the others; and know that it should have six splints or arms in many dispositions: whether the breakage is in one bone, or two; and strain it more above the breakage than elsewhere, and always less away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the drapes be on top of the breakage soft and moist, not hard nor dry; and let the cord, which holds it in place, be linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident happens to the member, such as itching which comes to the member, then it is necessary that you bathe the member in hot water, until those itchings are calmed down; and let the member not at all remain resting.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then recommence the stretching, and if the joint is softened and the bones are separated, and similar things, then adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the stiffness cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then it is necessary that you loosen it a little, and let it be like that for some days, until the stiffness goes away, and then strain.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said do not come to the patient, then do not untie for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or around it, then bind his hands to his neck, and let his necks be equal, and beware of movement and gesturing, and sleep on his back; and know that this bruise is restored in 30 days or 35, and by chance in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and as to the thumbs, there are many breakings, and it does not come but that pleasure comes many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged, and sit directly in front of him evenly; then put his hand on the stretched cloth, and stretch out the assistants to the broken bones, and set them equal with the mirror, until they are well joined; and apply the plaster and poultices, if abscesses do not come, then place a splint according to the size of the limb; and let it be wrapped in a cloth made of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the edge of the palm around the belly of the hand, then make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to wrap it around his broken hand; and then strain with a long cloth, and let the splint be as soft as the palm of the hand, and strain, as it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the far end, then it is necessary that you put a splint on top and another one below in the palm, so that the hand be open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and stop the joint between the thumbs.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of our thumbs, such as the index or one of the others, then set it straight and equal, as it is necessary; and strain with the palm, and if you see that you put a small straight splint to lift the break, and it does not move; and if the break is at the other thumb, then set it straight and equal, and tie it with the healthy thumb that comes after; or you tie them all together in one holding, as it seems best, or you put a splint on top, such as the pouchet; and take care of the restoration and the disposition of the hot abscess, and attend to what comes, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken toe
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the toe is many times broken, and it is well seen when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one thread is tied above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then stretches each assistant's thread to its equal part; and this is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near to the root of the heel, so that one of the ligaments points towards the armpit, and the other ligaments are below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, and then be the ligament below the knee, and be the extension downwards; then place the mirrors on the bone with both hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and tie it, lest abscesses come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, then let it be calmed first and then return to your work and care; the binding is done in the same manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the break with a bandage made of doubled cloth in two or three layers, and remove any superfluities; then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the knee, and insert a long thread between the heel and the leg, below the knee joint, and let it come out above; then turn up the bandage on the leg and heel; then place two or three estelas on the break, and one estela on the bone of the leg; then employ the eight threads between the leg and heel with soft drapery to put equal tension; then begin to tie firmly three turns or four around the break; and as you go up above the break, and less tension; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you have inserted between the leg and heel, and tie three estelas above; then come back down below to the head of the thread, until you reach the foot; and if it does not move from its place, then leave it so, lest an aposteme or swelling or other similar thing occur.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is, then loosen it, and adjust what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that pinch, then it is necessary to remove them if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut the flesh and draw out the force; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And once the crotch is broken like this, one puts stays in it, as in an aid and on the arm; however, in this restoration made, the patient does not ache.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the crotch is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversities of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the hollow of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the hollow of the knee there is often a small break, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, but only a slight crack or perforation occurs, and it happens to all wounds, and without wound, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one makes equal what is bent to its knees, so that it can be assembled as much as possible; then put the plaster, and I put a rounded stay, if you have need of it, and the straining as it should be, then reward all the dispositions that we have said in other breakages, such as aposteme, heat, and any such thing; then apply to each accident what is needed, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "malleolus" and the other "fibula"; and it has all sorts of breakage as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is equal with that of the arm, and the work is done there. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns every which way.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bone is broken, then turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the big bone is broken, one feels great pain and it can be seen well; and it turns downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then administer an extension and place it evenly, and tie the splints equally; but still, it is necessary if the break is ugly and there are many pieces that the extension be smaller and lighter; and loosen according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, then take two pieces of fust covered with linen that surround the leg on one side and the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee down to the ankle; then wrap in two places one bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle, and so the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and thus it is well; and some give a support of fust along the length of the leg, and it is of linen, and put the leg to prevent movement, and properly make what is in the breakage where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is aposteme, heat or any other accident; then cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not come from a breakage, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and bend a little, and there is no more harm than just stiffness in several positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot break, and you see these bones rising one above the other, then put the patient's foot on the ground, just as if they were about to walk, and then place your own foot beside theirs where the bones are lifted, and press down until they return to their places; then apply plaster and compresses above, and below the belly of the foot a small pad with two full sheets, then bind the foot properly, and when you have wrapped drapes around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days will have passed, then loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are some of the toes broken, then restore them, as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put on each broken toe a stay according to the length of the toe, and be a little bit wider, then place below the foot that pad which I said, and bind it properly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken toes, then put on each toe a stay according to its quantity, wrapped in one sheet of linen, and bind the pad below the foot; and let it be so that it holds well at the top of the pad above the belly of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you not forget the other things I have said about other breakages, as we have said; and take care of each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand of the man is broken or that of the woman, restore it thus as we have said in the book of the hare; and these breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and use there and attends my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break signifies to many the right way of restoration: listen then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the arm, when it is broken, take a goose's gizzard and insert it into the arm; then wrap cloth around it three days or more, and it will be healed hastily.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, even if it is great, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, to be healed immediately, so that the wounds that we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, and then remains raw with vitriol, or you have nothing else to do, then begin again to restore the break in the same hour, or on that same day, lest apostemes come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if apostemes come there, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the apostemes are calmed down, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring forth a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears on the surface above the skin uncovered, it is necessary that you put a small pin into it gently with your hands, at a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not prepared to be put in equal with your hands, then take this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight inches of length, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and for that reason it is necessary for the surgeon to take three or four, according as he needs them in each treatment of breakage; and be round and a little bit thick, so it does not bend much under compression on the member at your work, and be pointed forward, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which it is necessary that the curved nail be placed on top of the visible bone; and set it once, until it recedes, and be equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, it is necessary that you shape the top of the bone, so that the instruments have possession.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, then file it down with a suitable instrument, or chisel or scraper, to your ability; and then remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small scraps.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So it is in its place, then soak the cloth in black stiptic wine, and truly that is how to do it; and do not put anything on the wound except a compress or other dressing where there is oil, lest you bring forth rot and corruption; then administer the ointments when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, and cover all around with a bandage according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted by the break; and many times this has been done by foolish healers, and they have brought upon the patient death or corruption at times; and let the straining be gentler and more soothing than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil events may happen, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then it does not need to be put on with ointments; but instead, envelop around, in place of ointments, hard cloths and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the bow of the wound is growing, then take away what you put on top all wine, and place healing ointment on the wound, as with fourfold medicine and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is solidified and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be aligned in such a way that the bows bend downward slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it cannot heal but instead forms a bow, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which reason you must wash the wound with tent, and remove all these splintered bones that bring forth that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place or another manner of corruption, then you must cure it, according to what is written in its chapter before this.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the member, as with the hip or shoulder bone, and other similar great members, do not pull it out at once, for many times death ensues, but leave it until it can be set; by chance it will fall into place after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come on the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come across after the healing of the breakage, especially when it is near the jointure, and it is a sad thing to see the figure of the member; and by chance the member cannot perform its natural actions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take heed then if it is fresh: administer stiptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acaica, and similar others, in the way that you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with black wine or egg white or oil; and put them on the night in saucers, and strain it well, and do not remove it for three days; then release it, and begin another one, until the swellings are removed; or you may apply a piece of linen well made; for the properties of linen are such that they remove all swelling from the members; and if the nodation has already become hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then file down on top, and make the superfluity apparent; or have it removed by a barber, until it is removed, and cure it as long as it is needed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is restored and remains after the members are weak and subtle, it happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many ties, and could not come to the nourishment of the member; or due to excessive swelling; or due to very great movements, not in its time; or because it has a little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and have their body relaxed, until their blood is multiplied in them; and administer baths to them, and give them joy and ease; then apply poultice on the member, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and the swelling often with cool water, until the nourishment flows to the member; and restore it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The injured limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone broken open, and the form of the limb ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: so do not believe those who say one should break the limb all over again; many fools have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and great evils come from it, and sometimes even death; however, if the swellings and tortures are fresh, then they must be raised with hot water, or herbs that soften, such as dill leaves, roots, and mellilot, and similar things; and a mollifying plaster, like well-made dyaquilon, and take the juice of dill, and mix it with goose grease or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or take fat figs, and grind them with henbane fiber, and similar medicines that hasten the healing.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is loosened by constant and continuous rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be a gentle movement to the member each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and indurated like stone, and needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut all the way to the bone, lightly cutting with a subtle incision; and put attention and study into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	The book of dislocations begins here
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, then it must be brought back into place promptly.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Because if one delays, the swelling increases, and by chance, if one resets it with points at the swollen area; therefore it is not good to move it until it has subsided: many times spasms and other pains come; however, when this happens, make the patient well again, then leave them, until the abscess is fully appeased; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then gently realign it, and cure each member as the treatment comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters of dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	of jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It often happens that the jawbones are dislocated downwards, and the dislocation of both is in two ways: or they are slightly pulled out of their place and softened somewhat; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and the saliva from the mouth flows so much that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and wraps around his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in a few arrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you should realign it quickly, and do not delay; and in such a way that the assistants hold the patient's head, and put the mirror's pouch from one of their hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other two hands are free to make equal; and instruct the patient to relax his mandibles, and move them all around.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers place it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially if the two jawbones are together, then raise them with hot water and oil, until they reset slightly; nor delay in resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back even, and the patient's mouth closes well with a softening sensation, then place moist cloths on them in a wax made of rose oil and beeswax, and gently tie them with soft threads; and let the patient sleep on their back, and have their limbs between two cushions, so that they do not move to either side, nor make an effort to speak, but take light food, as long as the pains are gone, and the jawbones are numbed; and then eat what they want lightly, and do not trouble themselves with opening their mouth to eat and drink, until the jawbone is well numb and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be brought back to their place within an hour, and are not converted to their natural state, then fevers and severe constipation come, and by chance, dissolution of the bowels, and by chance, vomiting of pure gall.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a misfortune; and many times the person to whom it happens dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the shoulder
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot dislocate from the front side within its continuity and towards the chest, and is sometimes dislocated to the back, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and stretches out their arms; then presses the joint firmly onto your palm, and it will return; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it tight; and the bone that is opposite the cut cannot dislocate; if not, and if it does dislocate at any time, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and in the same way, bring back the bone of the shoulder when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: firstly, it dislocates towards the lower part of the armpit; secondly, it dislocates towards the back; and thirdly, it dislocates towards the upper part, which happens rarely; nor does it dislocate backwards for the shoulder or inside for the nerves; and many times it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for then it is done hastily; but in those who have enough flesh, it jumps at paces, and returns at paces.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they receive a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you examine it thoroughly until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocation occurs when it goes down towards the armpit, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest diversity; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and below the armpit to touch the head of the shoulder, just like it is an ox; and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its place nor move with any movements; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the touch; and this manner of dislocation is not suitable for returning when it is new or the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the servant lifts the patient's hand up high, then puts his fingers underneath it and lifts the jointure upwards to its place; and the servant lifts his hand and stretches it up high, then puts it underneath; so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in three days after, so it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and the attendant should rise up soothing and assuaging, like a decoction of althea and fenugrec and melilote in water, and should bring it; then the patient should be laid on their back, and a woolen pad equal, not too soft or too hard, should be placed under them, and the doctor should put their fingers on the patient's heel on the pad, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and draw the patient's hand; and another attendant should hold the patient's head so that it does not move downwards; now this shoulder is coming back, and if you see it in this manner: and then make sure a person who is bigger than the patient is present; and they should stand facing the coast, and push the patient's shoulder under the attendant on the pad, and lift the pad high so that the patient hangs in the air; and another attendant should draw the patient's hand down towards their belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he will bear with him something heavy, and the dislocation will come back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And one also remedies it in another way: and is this on long iron placed in the earth, from which the head will be as hot as a piston, and not too thick nor too narrow; then it should be put under the patient, but only after he has wrapped himself softly above, and the patient's hand should be stretched down below somewhat, and the jointure will return to its place promptly; and if it does not want to come back for all these things we have said, then do this cure: take a piece of iron from two arms and four fingers wide, which has the tip bent so as to fit easily into the crevice under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a soft cloth on top of the head of the wood, so that the wood does not hurt the patient, then place it underneath the shoulder blade of the patient; and stretch your arm up over the long wood, and hold the assistant's hand on top of the wood, and the arm to the tip of the hand; then put the arm on one shoulder of a board two fists in width, and let the hands hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so, in whatever way, then it is necessary that you put underneath the shoulder blade a sphere of equal wool, then place the poultice around with powder from the mill, with incense and an egg yolk, on all the shoulder and around; then stretch it underneath the shoulder blade gently, and turn the cloth over the poultice, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that you massage it little, until the limbs are comforted, for it will heal more quickly; and then massage more after five days or seven, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come in or for another reason, then it is necessary that you apply cauterization to three apertures, as shown before the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it does not hold after seven days, and the joint is not held, and cannot lift its arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the breast or the armpits, or behind, is caused by impulse and stretching of hands, and one should administer another treatment; and cure until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes swelling in the limb and delayed movement, then have the patient take many baths until that swelling is alleviated, and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the jointure of the shoulder is dislocated in points and comes back in points; and it has been dislocated from all parts, and indeed both before and behind, and the dislocation is not responded, because one sees well and feels well; and becomes dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the wound to the skin, so it can be seen clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is severed, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it as soon as the abscess comes to life, for if the abscess comes to life, then it would be grievous to reset; and by chance cannot be reset at all, especially when it is in the back; so it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and by chance death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is this: when it is such that one can reset it, then you stretch his hand to your two hands; and his arms should be spread out, and his hands of the mirror according to the shoulder around, above, and below, and push the joint into its places together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand to his own hand, and fixes at the root of the palm the shoulder that is displaced.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and this is because two ministers extend the arm, and hold it steady, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm on each side, when you have wrapped a double-length and wide cloth around it; and when the surgeon has joined the jointure to her hand, anoint the jointure with some oil to soften the jointure, then bind the jointure firmly, until it returns to its place; and when it is at its place, apply plaster dry with some egg, and bind it firmly, and leave the arm on the patient's neck for a few days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then separate the bond and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not fit well, then reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then separate it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	Et if he feels grievousness after the resetting of the joint, and it settles, so bathe him well and rub gently, and press until he is eased; or you put on the jointure a snow of fat sheep, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, soothly rub the jointure, then put the snow back on, and then enter the bath; and thus do twice or thrice, until he is healed; and if you see, so put on hay of moist cow's milk warmed with butter, and strain it on him; so he will return to his disposition.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and the swelling is light, more so than other joints Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place hastily, in the same hour that it dislocates, before the swelling becomes inflamed or an abscess forms hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is that you put the sick hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of the healthy hand, and have the patient place his palm on the appearance of the jointure, and press until it revives. Nevertheless, it is necessary to look if he is well in place; then put the patient's hand on a table at the stretching and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then the patient puts his back towards his hand on the table, and the doctor places his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, it is well; if not, then one should apply soothing poultices to abscesses and leave them in this way so as not to start again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains twisted; and no harm comes to the patient unless his hand is inflamed, and he cannot strain anything at all: then know that the nerves are strained or the arteries; so there is no other remedy than to strain by fire-cautery in this case, and by chance it may be of some use.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are in place, then put on the plaster that we have said, and strain it and leave it five days, then take it off and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some swelling, then apply warm water, and rub it until he is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the wrist of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or belly; then the finger remains and pushes the dislocation into its socket as far as it can come back, then supports the head of the finger and leads it towards the part where it is separated; and leaves it for two days, and then puts it in line on that day; and binds it with a bandage, just as we have said, and loosens it again from day to day, and makes it move, and relieves the bandage; and does this often until it is straight, and likewise does this when it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and does it in the same way as before, until it is healed; and likewise does this when it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the coccyx of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the coccyx of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, then there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or percussion or similar things, the ancient ways of cures speak in great words, where there is not much benefit at all; but I have shortened it according to my intention and formed instruments in various manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositey that comes to the pit of the belly before, there is no intelligence nor health; and similarly that which comes directly between two sides, and one cannot cure fever except for that which properly comes from behind, as I say; and it is that the patient lies stretched out on their back in an equal position, and has a strain below them, so they do not injure themselves; then place one tisserie on the head on the ground, and another by the feet, and tie two straps parallel to each other around the patient's shoulders, and at the hips, and at the knees; and the two attendants should know the straps, the one on the head and the others by the feet, between the two tisseries; and be well fastened, the tissiers as we have said, and the mirrors put their palms on the spine in a straight line, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a piece of wood three arms long, and hollow out the bottom part, and the patient should be lying on their side, and insert the top part of the wood under the skin, then place the middle part of the wood on the spine; and put the mirrors' feet on the other end of the wood, and press well until it returns to its place; and if you see, make the same turn that turns at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you put two brands at the head of the patient's arm, and two others towards their feet, and between each brand, a palm's breadth of wood length; and each brand has one pore, where the turn goes through, and the brands are firmly stuck in the ground so they don't move; and between each pair of brands is one turning brand, above which the turns go around, and there are two small brands of a palm's breadth to turn the turn; and then tie the cord that is among the rings at the head turn towards the chief, and the other cord towards the feet at the other turn, and each of the servants turns their turn all along the cord, and the master sets the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, and then she puts poultices drying with abundance of eggwhite, and then binds it, and then makes an incision of a tablet of three fingers in length, that it occupy the place of the hipbone and the part of the spinal bone, so that the patient be sound; and if nothing comes at the end of healing, then one must administer soothing and soft medicines with the instrument we have said before; and sometimes one gives a piece of cloth, and sometimes an appearance appears in the back of the spine on the back, and one thinks it is dislocation; and that is the bone which opens, for which one should not presume at all: by chance death may come.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder do not come together except in dislocation alone, nor does it happen like with other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to three parts: inward and outward, and before and behind; and more inwardly than outwardly, and less dislocated before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is that when you join the ailing leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens up more to the patient's knee than the healthy one, and the ailing patient cannot double their knee over the fire; and the swelling is in the place below an abscess hot, because the head of the groin comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it happens outward is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it happens before is that his leg is well-shaped according to completion; however, he does not bend his knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot do so beforehand, and retains his urine, and swells the groin, and when he walks, it passes above the ankle.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it happens behind is that he cannot spread his knee, nor bend it, and is that leg more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and is the head of the crix at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.
